CONSENT CALENDAR
All matters listed under the Consent Calendar are considered by the Council to be routine and will be enacted by one motion without
discussion. If discussion is desired, that item may be removed and considered separately.
 
1.

Adopt a Resolution to reallocate an Executive Assistant position to Communications and Public Relations Analyst
position in Parks and Recreation.
CEQA: This reclassification is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative
activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section
15378(b)(5).)
2.
On-Call Building Support Services – Agreements and Budget Amendment
Adopt a Resolution to amend the Community Development Department’s fiscal year 2022-23 operating budget
to appropriate $540,000 of committed fund balance from the Construction Services Fund and increase the line
item for professional services to a total of $1,000,000; approve on-call professional services agreements with
4Leaf, Inc., CSG Consultants, Inc., Interwest Consulting Group, Inc., True North Compliance Services, Inc. for on-
call building support services for terms of approximately 3.5 years, with compensation not to exceed $2,000,000
per agreement; and authorize the Community Development Director to execute the agreements in substantially
the form presented.

On-Call Historic Evaluations for Various Projects – Agreements
Approve agreements with Architecture and History, LLC, Architectural Resources Group, and Page & Turnbull for
historic resource evaluation and review for terms of approximately 5 years in an amount not to exceed $500,000,
and authorize the Community Development Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form
presented.
CEQA: This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity
that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)
(5).)
4.
2022-23 Community Development Block Grant Project – Appropriation and Agreement
Adopt a Resolution to authorize the appropriation of funds in the amount of $105,000 from the Community
Development Block Grant Fund reserve balance to the Community Development Block Grant Projects budget;
award an agreement to Precision Emprise, LLC dba Precision Concrete Cutting for the 2022-23 Community
Development Block Grant Project in the amount of $334,171.60; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of
$35,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented
and issue change orders as allowed by the contract and within the contingency amount.
CEQA: This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or
former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
5.
2nd and El Camino Parking Garage Elevator Modernization – Contract
Award a construction contract to Urban Elevator Service CA, LLC for construction to improve the elevator at the
2nd and El Camino parking garage for $375,390; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $56,000; and
authorize the Public Works Director to execute the contract in substantially the form presented and issue change
orders within the contingency amount.
CEQA: This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA
Guidelines Section 15301.)
6.
Delaware Street Relief Sewer – Interagency Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 2 to the Service Agreement with the Peninsula Corridor Joint Powers Board for the
Delaware Street Relief Sewer project in the amount of $74,017, for a revised total agreement amount of
$218,275.96, and authorize the Mayor to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: The work addressed by this administrative report is being undertaken to support the Clean Water Program.
This project is subject to the requirements of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), the general
components of which are included as part of the Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR)
(SCH No. 201532006) that was prepared for the Clean Water Program. The Final PEIR was certified by City Council
on June 6, 2016.

PUBLIC HEARING
City Council action on the following public hearing(s) represents a final decision concluding all administrative proceedings. Judicial
review may be had only if a petition is filed with the Court not later than the 90th day following the date the decision is made.
Judicial review of environmental determinations may be subject to a time period for litigation as short as 30 days following the date
the decision is made.

PREPARED BY:
Parks and Recreation Department
MEETING DATE:
January 17, 2023 
SUBJECT:
Parks and Recreation Department – Position Reallocation
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to reallocate an Executive Assistant position to Communications and Public Relations Analyst position 
in Parks and Recreation.
BACKGROUND:
Per San Mateo Municipal Code Section 2.57.030(d), classification revisions become effective upon approval by the City 
Council. Since 2018, the Parks and Recreation Department has had a vacant Executive Assistant position. The reallocation 
of this position to a Communications and Public Relations Analyst is requested to reflect the department’s needs and 
higher level of responsibilities that are required. As the local community grows and becomes more diverse, the Parks and 
Recreation Department has become aware of the mounting need for communications management. It is imperative that 
the department creates accurate, appropriately branded and personalized outreach material to build public awareness 
about our programs, events, and projects, as well as to engage the public in matters that are most important to them. 
Having a lead staff person in this role will ensure that the department is always aligned with the City’s overall messaging 
goals. The department currently directs several staff to create outreach material, which results in conflicting priorities and 
delivery challenges, and often times updates have not been timely and messaging has been outdated or misleading. This 
has highlighted the need for a focused position to be engaged, maximizing the outreach efforts of the department, crafting 
the necessary media and engagement strategy and ensuring that our information is current, accurate and our patronage 
maximized.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The expected budget impact is estimated at $54,000 annually.  Any budget necessary to fill this position in the current 
fiscal year will be absorbed within the department’s operating budget.  The Communications and Public Relations Analyst 
position will then be fully budgeted in the 2023-24 operating budget.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This reclassification is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 - Proposed Resolution

SUBJECT:
On-Call Building Support Services – Agreements and Budget Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to amend the Community Development Department’s fiscal year 2022-23 operating budget to 
appropriate $540,000 of committed fund balance from the Construction Services Fund and increase the line item for 
professional services to a total of $1,000,000; approve on-call professional services agreements with 4Leaf, Inc., CSG 
Consultants, Inc., Interwest Consulting Group, Inc., True North Compliance Services, Inc. for on-call building support 
services for terms of approximately 3.5 years, with compensation not to exceed $2,000,000 per agreement; and authorize 
the Community Development Director to execute the agreements in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
Over the last several years, the Community Development Department (CDD) has utilized consultants for a number of 
different specialized services within the Building Division. These services are frequently utilized in response to unexpected 
staff shortages or due to a high volume of development in the City. Recently, the Building Division has experienced both an 
unusual number of vacancies in key positions and a high volume of permit applications, particularly for large 
developments. As a result, and to ensure the City is prepared for similar circumstances in the future, CDD issued a request 
for qualifications (RFQ) in August 2022 to identify multiple firms capable of providing specialized building support services 
on an on-call basis. 
The RFQ identified a number of areas where the Building Division anticipated a future need for professional services and 
allowed interested firms to submit statements of qualifications for any or all of those identified needs. In total, the City 
received responses from seven firms and evaluated those submissions based on the firms’ understanding of the work 
involved, prior experience with similar work, quality and technical ability of the proposed staff, and the pricing structure. 
Ultimately, CDD staff utilized those criteria and a check of references to identify four firms to provide on-call building 
support services. Together, these firms provide a broad range of services and cover all areas CDD identified as potential 
Building Division needs in the RFQ. The four firms are:
•
4LEAF, Inc.
•
CSG Consultants, Inc.
•
Interwest Consulting Group, Inc.
•
True North Compliance Services, Inc.
To manage the on-call contracts, staff will identify the firm best positioned to provide the needed services and develop 
specific scopes of work and budgets for any work performed. 
9 of 274

--- page 10 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
BUDGET IMPACT:
For fiscal year 2022-23, CDD budgeted a total of $460,000 for professional services spending from the City’s Construction 
Services Fund. Given current staffing limitations and the extremely high volume of permit applications, the Department is 
requesting an additional $540,000 in the fiscal year 2022-23 budget, for a total of $1,000,000 to cover professional services 
costs. This request can be absorbed by the Construction Services Fund’s balance and coincides with a significant increase in 
revenue during the current fiscal year. 
Moving forward, the professional services provided through these on-call contracts will be accounted for within CDD’s 
annual operating budget. For some services, including plan check, each firm has a pricing structure that charges a percent 
of the City’s plan check fee, ensuring that the City will not be incurring costs that exceed the revenue brought in from 
building permit applications.  
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
These agreements and resolution are not projects subject to CEQA, because they are an organizational or administrative 
activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

Att 4 – Agreement with Interwest Consulting Group, Inc.

AGREEMENT WITH 4LEAF, INC.
FOR PROFESSIONAL CONSULTANT SERVICES
FOR 
ON-CALL BUILDING SUPPORT SERVICES
This Agreement, made and entered into this day of ____________________, by and between 
the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California 
(“CITY”), and 4LEAF, INC., a California Corporation (“CONSULTANT”), whose address is 2126 Rheem 
Drive, Pleasanton, CA 94588.
RECITALS:
A.  CITY desires certain on-call building support services hereinafter described.
B.  CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these on-call building support 
services by reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such services and CONSULTANT 
has offered to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.

Page 2 of 14

SECTION 3 - DUTIES OF CITY
CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project.
CITY shall examine documents submitted by CONSULTANT and shall render decisions pertaining 
thereto promptly, to avoid unreasonable delay in the progress of CONSULTANT's work.
SECTION 4 - TERM
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence on February 1, 2023 and 
be completed on June 30, 2026.
SECTION 5 - PAYMENT
Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment 
request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full 
performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONSULTANT a fee in an amount 
not to exceed $2,000,000, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this Agreement, attached and 
incorporated by reference.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS
All documents prepared by CONSULTANT in the performance of this Agreement, although 
instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not.

SECTION 8 - CONFIDENTIALITY
All reports and documents prepared by CONSULTANT in connection with the performance of 
this Agreement are confidential until released by CITY to the public.  CONSULTANT shall not make any 
such documents or information available to any individual or organization not employed by 
CONSULTANT or CITY without the written consent of CITY before any such release.
SECTION 9 - INTEREST OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT covenants that it presently has no interest, and shall not acquire any interest, 
direct or indirect, financial or otherwise, which would conflict in any manner or degree with the 
performance of the services under this Agreement.
SECTION 10 - CONSULTANT'S STATUS
It is expressly agreed that in the performance of the professional services required under this 
Agreement, CONSULTANT shall at all times be considered an independent contractor as defined in 
Labor Code Section 3353, under control of the CITY as to the result of the work but not the means by 
which the result is accomplished.  Nothing herein shall be construed to make CONSULTANT an agent or 
employee of CITY while providing services under this Agreement.
SECTION 11 - INDEMNITY
CONSULTANT agrees to hold harmless and indemnify CITY, its elected and appointed officials, 
employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense arising 
out of CONSULTANT’s performance of this Agreement, except those claims arising out of CITY’s sole 
negligence or willful misconduct.  CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and appointed 
officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. The CONSULTANT’S duty to indemnify shall 
survive expiration or early termination of this Agreement.
SECTION 12 - INSURANCE
CONSULTANT shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract and three years 
thereafter (five years for building or major improvements) the insurance specified in Exhibit C to this 
Agreement.

SECTION 13 - NON-ASSIGNABILITY
Both parties hereto recognize that this Agreement is for the personal services of CONSULTANT 
and cannot be transferred, assigned, or subcontracted by CONSULTANT without the prior written 
consent of CITY.
SECTION 14 - RELIANCE UPON PROFESSIONAL
SKILL OF CONSULTANT
It is mutually understood and agreed by and between the parties hereto that CONSULTANT is 
skilled in the professional calling necessary to perform the work agreed to be done under this 
Agreement and that CITY relies upon the skill of CONSULTANT to do and perform the work in the most 
skillful manner, and CONSULTANT agrees to thus perform the work.  The acceptance of CONSULTANT's 
work by CITY does not operate as a release of CONSULTANT from said obligation.
SECTION 15 - WAIVERS
The waiver by either party of any breach or violation of any term, covenant, or condition of this 
Agreement or of any provisions of any ordinance or law shall not be deemed to be a waiver of such 
term, covenant, condition, ordinance or law or of any subsequent breach or violation of the same or of 
any other term, condition, ordinance, or law.  The subsequent acceptance by either party of any fee or 
other money which may become due hereunder shall not be deemed to be a waiver of any preceding 
breach or violation by the other party of any term, covenant, or condition of this Agreement or of any 
applicable law or ordinance.
SECTION 16 - SEVERABILITY
If any term or portion of this Agreement is held to be invalid, illegal, or otherwise 
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall 
continue in full force and effect.
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.

SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with

bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.
SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
1. Scope of Services 
Consultant shall provide thorough, accurate, and professional services as follows:
i.
Plan Check/Review Services 
Consultant shall perform plan check/review services as requested by the City’s 
Community Development Director or designee. All plan review services provided by 
Consultant shall include the initial plan review and all subsequent review cycles as 
necessary for building permit issuance, as well as revisions submitted after issuance, 
while adhering to the City’s standard turnaround time.
ii.
Building Inspection Services 
Consultant shall perform building inspection services for a specified number of hours as 
requested by the City’s Community Development Director or designee. These services 
shall include review of all approved plans, specifications, documents; review and 
respond to all inspection requests and reports; attend mandatory meetings; perform 
inspections for compliance to applicable State of California Building, Mechanical, 
Electrical, Plumbing, Fire codes, as well as State energy efficiency and accessibility 
standards as amended by the City of San Mateo.
iii.
Permit Technician Services 
Consultant shall perform permit technician services for a specific number of hours as 
requested by the City’s Community Development Director or designee. These services 
shall include accepting and screening building permit applications for completeness, 
conformance with building codes, ordinances and department standards, policies, and 
guidelines; and technical support related to screening of building and planning permit 
applications.
iv.
Code Enforcement Services 
Consultant shall perform code enforcement services for a specified number of hours as 
requested by the City’s Community Development Director or designee. These services 
shall include reviewing complaints and performing inspections of properties for the 
compliance of the following adopted technical codes with San Mateo local 
amendments:
•
California Building Codes
•
International Property Maintenance Code
•
California Health and Safety Code Division 13 Housing – Part 1.5 Regulations of 
Buildings Used for Human Habitation
•
San Mateo Municipal Code, department standards, policies, and guidelines
v.
Certified Access Specialist (CASp) Services 
Consultant shall perform certified access specialist services as requested by the City’s 
Community Development Director or designee. These services shall include reviewing 
plans and specifications for CASp requirements; making field inspections for compliance 
19 of 274

--- page 20 ---
Professional Services
Page 9 of 14
Rev 9/22
with CASp and other accessibility code requirements; providing technical advice on 
accessibility issues as they arise.

Rates are inclusive of “tools of the trade” such as forms, telephones, and consumables.
•
All invoicing will be submitted monthly.
•
Staff Augmentation work (excluding plan review) is subject to 4-hour minimum charges unless stated 
otherwise. Services billed in 4-hour increments.  
•
Most plan reviews will be done in 10 business days or less and 5 business days or less for re-checks. This 
is not inclusive of holidays or the day of the pick-up of plans.
•
Expedited reviews will be billed at 1.5x the plan review fee listed in the fee schedule. Return time will be 
within seven (7) days of receipt of the plans from the City. 
•
Plan review of deferred submittals & revisions will be billed at the hourly rates listed. 
•
All plan review services will be subject to a $250.00 minimum fee if percentage-based fee or two (2) hour 
minimum charge if hourly rates apply. 
•
Larger complex plan reviews can be negotiated to achieve the best possible pricing. 4LEAF has a proven 
track record of working with municipalities to provide expedited reviews with discounted pricing when 
applicable.
•
All plan review services are billed on a percentage basis and includes the initial review and two (2) 
rechecks.
-
Plan reviews will be billed on an hourly basis only after the initial review and two (2) rechecks 
unless otherwise agreed upon on a case-by-case basis.
-
Fire and Civil Reviews are billed on an hourly basis and are not included in our plan review 
percentage.
•
4LEAF assumes that these rates reflect the FY2022-2023 contract period. 3% escalation for FY2023-2024 
and FY2024-2025 is negotiable per market conditions.

Plan Review Turn-Around Times
4LEAF has a tremendous reputation for completing projects on-time and under budget. 4LEAF’s plan review team

these timeframes are negotiable based on your needs. At no additional cost, 4LEAF staff will transport the plans 
to and from the City  upon a phone call to the 4LEAF office or simply e-mail for “pick-up” to pickup@4leafinc.com.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).

Professional Services
Page 14 of 14
Rev 9/22
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

RECITALS:
A.  CITY desires certain on-call building support services hereinafter described.
B.  CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these on-call building support 
services by reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such services and CONSULTANT 
has offered to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT

coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.

Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.

Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.

Professional Services

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
1. Scope of Services 
Consultant shall provide thorough, accurate, and professional services as follows:
i.
Plan Check/Review Services 
Consultant shall perform plan check/review services as requested by the City’s 
Community Development Director or designee. All plan review services provided by 
Consultant shall include the initial plan review and all subsequent review cycles as 
necessary for building permit issuance, as well as revisions submitted after issuance, 
while adhering to the City’s standard turnaround time.
ii.
Building Inspection Services 
Consultant shall perform building inspection services for a specified number of hours as 
requested by the City’s Community Development Director or designee. These services 
shall include review of all approved plans, specifications, documents; review and 
respond to all inspection requests and reports; attend mandatory meetings; perform 
inspections for compliance to applicable State of California Building, Mechanical, 
Electrical, Plumbing, Fire codes, as well as State energy efficiency and accessibility 
standards as amended by the City of San Mateo.
iii.
Permit Technician Services 
Consultant shall perform permit technician services for a specific number of hours as 
requested by the City’s Community Development Director or designee. These services 
shall include accepting and screening building permit applications for completeness, 
conformance with building codes, ordinances and department standards, policies, and 
guidelines; and technical support related to screening of building and planning permit 
applications.
iv.
Code Enforcement Services 
Consultant shall perform code enforcement services for a specified number of hours as 
requested by the City’s Community Development Director or designee. These services 
shall include reviewing complaints and performing inspections of properties for the 
compliance of the following adopted technical codes with San Mateo local 
amendments:
•
California Building Codes
•
International Property Maintenance Code
•
California Health and Safety Code Division 13 Housing – Part 1.5 Regulations of 
Buildings Used for Human Habitation
•
San Mateo Municipal Code, department standards, policies, and guidelines
v.
Certified Access Specialist (CASp) Services 
Consultant shall perform certified access specialist services as requested by the City’s 
Community Development Director or designee. These services shall include reviewing 
plans and specifications for CASp requirements; making field inspections for compliance 
33 of 274

Page 9 of 12

with CASp and other accessibility code requirements; providing technical advice on 
accessibility issues as they arise.

FEE SCHEDULE
CSG’s fee schedule which includes fees for personnel providing the proposed scope of work is 
provided in the table below. We will coordinate the pickup and return of all plans via CSG staff or a 
licensed courier service.
Plan review based on a percentage of plan check fees includes initial plan review and two subsequent 
reviews. Additional reviews, deferred submittals, revisions and RFIs will be charged at the appropriate 
hourly rate below. RFIs for larger developments will be performed at an hourly rate, and turnaround 
times will be agreed upon in advance with the City.

All hourly rates include salaries, benefits, workers compensation insurance, local travel and miscellaneous office expenses. 
Should the scope of work change, or circumstances develop which necessitate special handling, CSG will notify the City prior 
to proceeding. Overtime services will be billed at 1.5x the applicable hourly rate. On July 1 of each year following the contract 
start date, CSG will increase hourly rates based on change in CPI for the applicable region. CSG will mail an invoice every 
month for services rendered during the previous month. Unless otherwise agreed, payment terms are 30-days from receipt 
of invoice.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
36 of 274

--- page 37 ---
Professional Services
Page 12 of 12
Rev 9/22
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

AGREEMENT WITH INTERWEST CONSULTING GROUP, INC.
FOR PROFESSIONAL CONSULTANT SERVICES
FOR 
ON-CALL BUILDING SUPPORT SERVICES
This Agreement, made and entered into this day of ____________________, by and between 
the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California 
(“CITY”), and INTERWEST CONSULTING GROUP, INC., a wholly owned subsidiary of SAFEbuilt, LLC 
(“CONSULTANT”), whose address 444 N Cleveland Ave, Loveland, CO 80537 .
RECITALS:
A.  CITY desires certain on-call building support services hereinafter described.
B.  CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these on-call building support 
services by reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such services and CONSULTANT 
has offered to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.
38 of 274

--- page 39 ---
Professional Services
Page 2 of 12
Rev 9/22
SECTION 3 - DUTIES OF CITY
CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project.
CITY shall examine documents submitted by CONSULTANT and shall render decisions pertaining 
thereto promptly, to avoid unreasonable delay in the progress of CONSULTANT's work.
SECTION 4 - TERM
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence on January 17th, 2023 and 
be completed on June 30, 2026.
SECTION 5 - PAYMENT
Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment 
request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full 
performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONSULTANT a fee in an amount 
not to exceed $2,000,000, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this Agreement, attached and 
incorporated by reference.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS
All documents prepared by CONSULTANT in the performance of this Agreement, although 
instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not. Notwithstanding any provisions of this Agreement to the 
contrary, pre-existing intellectual property of CONSULTANT, including any software owned or licensed 
by CONSULTAN, and any improvements thereto shall remain or become property of CONSULTANT.

SECTION 8 - CONFIDENTIALITY
All reports and documents prepared by CONSULTANT in connection with the performance of 
this Agreement are confidential until released by CITY to the public.  CONSULTANT shall not make any 
such documents or information available to any individual or organization not employed by 
CONSULTANT or CITY without the written consent of CITY before any such release.
SECTION 9 - INTEREST OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT covenants that it presently has no interest, and shall not acquire any interest, 
direct or indirect, financial or otherwise, which would conflict in any manner or degree with the 
performance of the services under this Agreement.
SECTION 10 - CONSULTANT'S STATUS
It is expressly agreed that in the performance of the professional services required under this 
Agreement, CONSULTANT shall at all times be considered an independent contractor as defined in 
Labor Code Section 3353, under control of the CITY as to the result of the work but not the means by 
which the result is accomplished.  Nothing herein shall be construed to make CONSULTANT an agent or 
employee of CITY while providing services under this Agreement.
SECTION 11 - INDEMNITY
CONSULTANT agrees to hold harmless and indemnify, defend CITY, its elected and appointed 
officials, employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and 
expense arising out of CONSULTANT’s performance of this Agreement, except those claims arising out 
of CITY’s sole negligence or willful misconduct.  CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and 
appointed officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. For the avoidance of doubt, 
CONSULTANT shall have the right to defend any action for which indemnification is sought under any 
part of this Section 11. Any person or entity seeking indemnification under this Section 11 shall 
promptly report the matter to CONSULTANT such that defense of the matter is not compromised. The 
CONSULTANT’S duty to indemnify shall survive expiration or early termination of this Agreement.
SECTION 12 - INSURANCE
CONSULTANT shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract and three years 
thereafter (five years for building or major improvements) the insurance specified in Exhibit C to this 
Agreement.

SECTION 13 - NON-ASSIGNABILITY
Both parties hereto recognize that this Agreement is for the personal services of CONSULTANT 
and cannot be transferred, assigned, or subcontracted by CONSULTANT without the prior written 
consent of CITY, which consent shall not be unreasonably delayed or withheld. 
SECTION 14 - RELIANCE UPON PROFESSIONAL
SKILL OF CONSULTANT
It is mutually understood and agreed by and between the parties hereto that CONSULTANT is 
skilled in the professional calling necessary to perform the work agreed to be done under this 
Agreement and that CITY relies upon the skill of CONSULTANT to do and perform the work in the most 
skillful manner, and CONSULTANT agrees to thus perform the work.  The acceptance of CONSULTANT's 
work by CITY does not operate as a release of CONSULTANT from said obligation.
SECTION 15 - WAIVERS
The waiver by either party of any breach or violation of any term, covenant, or condition of this 
Agreement or of any provisions of any ordinance or law shall not be deemed to be a waiver of such 
term, covenant, condition, ordinance or law or of any subsequent breach or violation of the same or of 
any other term, condition, ordinance, or law.  The subsequent acceptance by either party of any fee or 
other money which may become due hereunder shall not be deemed to be a waiver of any preceding 
breach or violation by the other party of any term, covenant, or condition of this Agreement or of any 
applicable law or ordinance.
SECTION 16 - SEVERABILITY
If any term or portion of this Agreement is held to be invalid, illegal, or otherwise 
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall 
continue in full force and effect.
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.

SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with 
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONSULTANT nor any of its 
subcontractors shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national 
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.
SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.
SECTION 21 - NOTICES
All notices hereunder shall be given in writing and mailed, postage prepaid, addressed as 
follows:

INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
1. Scope of Services 
Consultant shall provide thorough, accurate, and professional services as follows:
i.
Plan Check/Review Services 
Consultant shall perform plan check/review services as requested by the City’s 
Community Development Director or designee. All plan review services provided by 
Consultant shall include the initial plan review and all subsequent review cycles as 
necessary for building permit issuance, as well as revisions submitted after issuance, 
while adhering to the City’s standard turnaround time.
ii.
Building Inspection Services 
Consultant shall perform building inspection services for a specified number of hours as 
requested by the City’s Community Development Director or designee. These services 
shall include review of all approved plans, specifications, documents; review and 
respond to all inspection requests and reports; attend mandatory meetings; perform 
inspections for compliance to applicable State of California Building, Mechanical, 
Electrical, Plumbing, Fire codes, as well as State energy efficiency and accessibility 
standards as amended by the City of San Mateo.
iii.
Permit Technician Services 
Consultant shall perform permit technician services for a specific number of hours as 
requested by the City’s Community Development Director or designee. These services 
shall include accepting and screening building permit applications for completeness, 
conformance with building codes, ordinances and department standards, policies, and 
guidelines; and technical support related to screening of building and planning permit 
applications.
iv.
Code Enforcement Services 
Consultant shall perform code enforcement services for a specified number of hours as 
requested by the City’s Community Development Director or designee. These services 
shall include reviewing complaints and performing inspections of properties for the 
compliance of the following adopted technical codes with San Mateo local 
amendments:
•
California Building Codes
•
International Property Maintenance Code
•
California Health and Safety Code Division 13 Housing – Part 1.5 Regulations of 
Buildings Used for Human Habitation
•
San Mateo Municipal Code, department standards, policies, and guidelines
v.
Arborist Services 
Consultant shall perform arborist services as requested by the City’s Community 
Development Director or designee. These services shall include reviewing plans, 
planning applications, arborist reports, and tree protection plans for adherence to best 
57 of 274

--- page 58 ---
Professional Services
Page 9 of 13
Rev 9/22
management practices; prepare draft conditions of approval; and assist with tree 
ordinance updates, as required.
vi.
Certified Access Specialist (CASp) Services 
Consultant shall perform certified access specialist services as requested by the City’s 
Community Development Director or designee. These services shall include reviewing 
plans and specifications for CASp requirements; making field inspections for compliance 
with CASp and other accessibility code requirements; providing technical advice on 
accessibility issues as they arise.

INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).

Community Development Department
MEETING DATE:
January 17, 2023 
SUBJECT:
On-Call Historic Evaluations for Various Projects – Agreements
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve agreements with Architecture and History, LLC, Architectural Resources Group, and Page & Turnbull for historic 
resource evaluation and review for terms of approximately 5 years in an amount not to exceed $500,000, and authorize 
the Community Development Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The Community Development Department (CDD) frequently utilizes consultants to provide several specialized services 
within the Planning Division. Given the volume of planning applications CDD receives, Planning works with consultants on 
an as-needed basis based on the complexity and specific needs of an application. To expand the group of consultants 
available to the City, in September 2022, CDD issued a request for qualifications (RFQ) to identify multiple firms capable of 
providing specialized planning support services on an on-call basis.
The RFQ identified several areas where CDD anticipated needs based on the current applications in the pipeline, or past 
precedent, and allowed interested firms to submit statements of qualifications for any or all of those identified needs. One 
of the most-frequently utilized services is a historic resources evaluation, which is required for certain projects as dictated 
by the City’s municipal code or the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA). The City received six responses for this 
particular service and evaluated those submissions based on the firms’ understanding of the work involved, prior 
experience, quality and technical ability of the proposed staff, and pricing structure. Ultimately, CDD staff utilized those 
criteria to identify the following three firms to provide on-call historic evaluations:
•
Architecture + History, LLC
•
Architectural Resources Group
•
Page & Turnbull
The term of the proposed contracts will end June 30, 2028, and each has a not-to-exceed amount of $500,000. To manage 
the on-call contracts, staff will identify the firm best positioned to provide the needed services and develop specific scopes 
of work and budgets for any work performed. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Any work completed that is tied to a specific planning application is paid for by the applicant. Should any of the 
consultants perform work for the City, it will be accounted for within CDD’s annual operating budget.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
63 of 274

--- page 64 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS

Att 2 – Agreement with Architectural Resources Group
Att 3 – Agreement with Page & Turnbull

and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Assist the City of San Mateo Community Development Department with the following on an on-call 
basis:
•
Historic Resource Evaluations (HREs) for potential historic resources per the California 
Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) by applying the national, state, or local criteria of evaluation 
for listing
•
Mills Act requests
•

Secretary of Interior Standards
•
General consultation and support on City initiated historic preservation projects, historic code 
and policy updates, and other related historic topics.
•
Peer reviews of HREs and other historic documents prepared by other historic professionals

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.

Rev 9/22
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

AGREEMENT WITH ARCHITECTURAL RESOURCES GROUP
FOR PROFESSIONAL CONSULTANT SERVICES
FOR 
HISTORIC CONSULTATION AND EVALUATION SERVICES
This Agreement, made and entered into this day of ____________________, by and between 
the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California 
(“CITY”), and ARCHITECTURAL RESOURCES GROUP, a corporation (“CONSULTANT”), whose address is 
Pier 9, The Embarcadero, Suite 107, San Francisco, CA 94111.
RECITALS:
A.  CITY desires certain on-call historic consultation and evaluation services hereinafter 
described.
B.  CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these on-call historic consultation 
and evaluation services by reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such services and 
CONSULTANT has offered to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth 
herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.
76 of 274

--- page 77 ---
Professional Services
Page 2 of 11
Rev 9/22
SECTION 3 - DUTIES OF CITY
CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project.
CITY shall examine documents submitted by CONSULTANT and shall render decisions pertaining 
thereto promptly, to avoid unreasonable delay in the progress of CONSULTANT's work.
SECTION 4 - TERM
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence on January 17th, 2023 and 
be completed on June 30, 2028.
SECTION 5 - PAYMENT
Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment 
request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full 
performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONSULTANT a fee in an amount 
not to exceed $500,000, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this Agreement, attached and 
incorporated by reference.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS
All documents prepared by CONSULTANT in the performance of this Agreement, although 
instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not.

SECTION 8 - CONFIDENTIALITY

this Agreement are confidential until released by CITY to the public.  CONSULTANT shall not make any 
such documents or information available to any individual or organization not employed by 
CONSULTANT or CITY without the written consent of CITY before any such release.
SECTION 9 - INTEREST OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT covenants that it presently has no interest, and shall not acquire any interest, 
direct or indirect, financial or otherwise, which would conflict in any manner or degree with the 
performance of the services under this Agreement.
SECTION 10 - CONSULTANT'S STATUS
It is expressly agreed that in the performance of the professional services required under this

employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense arising 
out of CONSULTANT’s performance of this Agreement, except those claims arising out of CITY’s sole 
negligence or willful misconduct.  CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and appointed 
officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. The CONSULTANT’S duty to indemnify shall 
survive expiration or early termination of this Agreement.

Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.

name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once

If any term or portion of this Agreement is held to be invalid, illegal, or otherwise 
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall 
continue in full force and effect.
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.

SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with 
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONSULTANT nor any of its 
subcontractors shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national 
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.
SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Assist the City of San Mateo Community Development Department with the following on an on-call 
basis:
•
Historic Resource Evaluations (HREs) for potential historic resources per the California 
Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) by applying the national, state, or local criteria of evaluation 
for listing
•
Mills Act requests
•
Design review for historic resources that are proposed for alteration to be in compliance with 
Secretary of Interior Standards
•
General consultation and support on City initiated historic preservation projects, historic code 
and policy updates, and other related historic topics.
•
Peer reviews of HREs and other historic documents prepared by other historic professionals

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
